  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a31bda78-fe86-4259-a2da-eb8cf3c6e298'
      });
    }

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169295857" />
    <a title="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73227612-tina-the-girl-who-lives-in-fandoms"><img alt="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527940584p2/73227612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2169295857?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " href="/user/show/73227612-tina-the-girl-who-lives-in-fandoms">Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780743437332" href="/book/show/833709.The_Never_War">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2169295857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3292392893156640247"><b>4.25 Golden Stars</b><br/><br/>I loved this one, but I don't know I always felt the lack of something in this book, I don't know what it is; the premise & everything is Great, but maybe after Cloral & all those water technology in that territory, the lack of extraordinary stuff? maybe because it's more Historical than Fantasy? maybe I expected more...<br/><br/>but still awesome, thrilling of chases & so much FUN, I was chocking on laughter. it's kind of unfair that I could've given it 5 stars (comparing to some of my 5</span>
  <span id="freeText3292392893156640247" style="display:none"><b>4.25 Golden Stars</b><br /><br />I loved this one, but I don't know I always felt the lack of something in this book, I don't know what it is; the premise &amp; everything is Great, but maybe after Cloral &amp; all those water technology in that territory, the lack of extraordinary stuff? maybe because it's more Historical than Fantasy? maybe I expected more...<br /><br />but still awesome, thrilling of chases &amp; so much FUN, I was chocking on laughter. it's kind of unfair that I could've given it 5 stars (comparing to some of my 5 stars, this one is much better), but I guess I can't convince myself to give my least favourite book in this series a 5-star, because I should have a way to show that. (my strict rating system, I know!)<br /><br />Bobby Pendragon is back home... kind of...<br /><br />New York City, 1937, the vintage picture of Earth,<br />two Travelers (one slowly maturing, one hothead) plus one (the Wise)<br />living the history, among a bunch of gangsters.<br />so many things happening!<br />ignition of WWII in the background<br />the moment of revelation<br />such an unexpected twist which gives the heroes such a difficult time (&amp; made me cry)<br />hanging in midair above New York city!<br /><br />fantastic characters as always, new &amp; old.<br />fun &amp; sarcasm, like always, await us<br /><br />I always loved how gently Pendragon matured. seeing sense, still making mistakes, but trying to learn his lessons.<br /><br />&amp; my intelligent Patrick's first appearance!<br /><br />I loved how it ended, it was beautiful.<br /><br />also in my 4th read, I noticed Bobby was actually the first main character who was a book lover, like me, &amp; the whole fanboy talking &amp; pop cultures references are awesome. I guess that's another reason why I love him!<br />&amp; for the first time, I finished it in only 1 day! just like book 1, a few years ago! yas! new record!<br /><br />Bobby's so cute on this cover!</span>

  <span id="freeText15471505347058915634" style="display:none"><i>What would you sacrifice for the greater good?</i><br /><br />Bobby and Spader travel to the territory known as First Earth to defeat Saint Dane in his latest scheme.<br /><br />-----<br /><br /><i>*screams obscenities*</i> far better than I remember<br /><b>AMAZING</b><br /><br /><u>What to know/ expect:</u><br />- a fast-paced adventure<br />- danger<br />- good characters and friend dynamics &lt;3<br />- these books do have a repeating pattern (but there's comfort in repetition :P )<br />- early 1900 US history, specifically 1937 (one of my favorite points in history)<br />- Saint Dane is such a good villain. at least I think so *eyes everyone suspiciously* he scared me as a child and he still scares me now<br />- quotes to make you think. ex: <i>"The future will always be here, it's the present we have to worry about."</i><br />- cool dudes<br />- gangsters (surprisingly they aren't exactly villains)<br />- some Nazis and swastikas (no durr, for this point in time)<br />- a glimpse into the future <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and a <i>VERY</i> realistic alternate future (I'm still terrified) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- the most relatable book in the series, it's more historical than fantasy<br />- my favorite of the series, <s>I hope you cry &gt;:D</s><br /><br />If this book is anything to go by, the <i>Pendragon</i> books are far more <b>awesome</b> than I remember.</span>

<div id="review_66063559" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66063559" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242771111p2/2299764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66063559?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/2299764-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66063559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17293599459660549292">I think what I love most about this series is the different worlds. Every book, there's a completely new setting to lose yourself in, complete with a new cast of characters. But of course, sometimes the best ones from previous novels come along for the ride.<br/><br/>Bobby Pendragon now finds himself in a very familiar territory indeed; First Earth, his home planet in the 1930's. And he quickly discovers that the "tipping point" here has everything to do with time. Somewhere, someone, helped along by none</span>
  <span id="freeText17293599459660549292" style="display:none">I think what I love most about this series is the different worlds. Every book, there's a completely new setting to lose yourself in, complete with a new cast of characters. But of course, sometimes the best ones from previous novels come along for the ride.<br /><br />Bobby Pendragon now finds himself in a very familiar territory indeed; First Earth, his home planet in the 1930's. And he quickly discovers that the "tipping point" here has everything to do with time. Somewhere, someone, helped along by none other than Saint Dane, is going to set something in motion that may become the catalyst for an event that will change history: World War II. And in order to save First Earth, Bobby will have to unravel the web of the past, the present, and the future, as well as make one of the most difficult choices ever.<br /><br />Accompanied by the complex, vengeful, charismatic Vo Spader from the previous novel, with the addition of First Earth's mellow and wise Traveler Gunny, Bobby has reached a personal tipping point of his own; the time when he will truly come to understand what it means to be a Traveler.<br /><br />I loved that this book took place in our own past, with all the time-appropriate references. I honestly used Google a couple times just to see if some of the characters Bobby met in the past were based on real people! Reading Bobby's incredulous, wondering account of experiencing all the time-travel was very realistic and consistant with his unique narrative voice. And as usual, the cliffhanger leaves you just like Bobby's ever-loyal friends Mark and Courtney; waiting for his next journal and his next adventure in a new territory.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17293599459660549292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2119563016" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2119563016" />
    <a title="Deviki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2484174-deviki"><img alt="Deviki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311927680p2/2484174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2119563016?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deviki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deviki" href="/user/show/2484174-deviki">Deviki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780743437332" href="/book/show/833709.The_Never_War">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=bookcover_extraordinaire">bookcover_extraordinaire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=books-i-enjoyed-reading">books-i-enjoyed-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=diversity_mixed">diversity_mixed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=time_travel-or_time_jump">time_travel-or_time_jump</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=science_fiction">science_fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=series_books">series_books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=white_men_boy">white_men_boy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=fantasy_mystery">fantasy_mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2119563016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14103220181123836753">Wow …..after reading this book ….........I was like “mindblown baby” I love love love how the author had cooperate a famous real life event to his fictional adventure story!!! I actually stopped reading the book to watched a documentary on that faithful event, on youtube. Because, I just have to know more! Learn plenty too :) <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456721773ra/18269303.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>You got to admit this book is quite different in a way but at the same time its still the same :P<br/>I'm really glad the author had decided to change the storytelling concept a</span>
  <span id="freeText14103220181123836753" style="display:none">Wow …..after reading this book ….........I was like “mindblown baby” I love love love how the author had cooperate a famous real life event to his fictional adventure story!!! I actually stopped reading the book to watched a documentary on that faithful event, on youtube. Because, I just have to know more! Learn plenty too :) <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456721773ra/18269303.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You got to admit this book is quite different in a way but at the same time its still the same :P<br>I'm really glad the author had decided to change the storytelling concept a lil differently this time because this book had a lot to information and a lot uncover mysteries. Saint Dane's evil plot or motive was quite different. I mean sure he plots to destroy any territories he step foot in but, as always his motive is to cause chaos and destroy the territory ! This time his motive is the same but it's aimed slightly differently at someone else in particular. <br><br>Ok, I'm jumping wayyy ahead now!! <br><br>The story starts off by tell us (from the Book two's end prologue) that Bobby had lost his ring and he is now writing his journal in a bundle and safe keeping it in a bank's deposit box. Decades later, Mike and Courtney get to read it, its like some kind of treasure hunt secret . The whole idea is SUPER COOL!! <br><br>Ok, so we come to understand that Saint Dane had flumed tricked Bobby and Spader into thinking that his next destination is Veelox. But we soon discover that the truth when we're briefly introduced to Aja (her head mostly), Traveler from Veelox. I like that we get to briefly meet other Travelers in this book like they are some kind of famous cameo actors in TV shows. <br><br>I'm starting to see a lil pattern in this book, like we get introduced to one Traveler and that Traveler kind of “follows” Bobby until he “exchange” the old one with a new one!? I don't know if I'm making sense but that's how I feel when I'm reading this book. <br><br>In Book 2 we are introduced to Spader, we've seen how Spader's emotions gets out of control and we have also seen the devastation it lead to. I like Spader, really, I do, but that guy needs to keep his emotion in check and “see” the bigger picture. That's the whole point of being a Traveler, for the greater good. So I knew, Spader's emotion is going to go out of control again. Funny though, sometimes the most happy-go-lucky person can also an emotional wreck. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506616518ra/24032563.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We are acquainted with First Earth Traveler, Gunny, I really like him, I find him to be smart, funny, loyal and totally dependable. You get this feeling that he will have your back no matter what! And it is reveal to be true later! At first I thought Gunny's role was like Press and Osa, that he was an experienced Traveler waiting to pick his Traveler heir, but I was surprised that he is the actually THE Traveler for First Earth! I mean he is an older man, not just by few months but years!!<br><br>Honestly, I had to stop reading this book at one point and start looking up pictures of New York and Manhattan from 1937, I had to see pictures of people back then and their lifestyle, just so I get a clear “representation” of what this First Earth is like. I mean really, it was interesting to learn something along the way :) <br><br>You know, I don't know how I would have made it in First Earth, because when Bobby was searching for clues, I had this urge to say …...”just google it Bobby !!” LOL. Because we live in an era where information is at our fingertips, and with Bobby' doing everything “manually” it was seriously “painful” to read LOL. I mean, they don't even have a TV !!<br><br>I think I liked that we are reading Bobby's journal continuously because I think it was so full of information and twisted plots, I would have gotten a bit annoyed if we are forced to take a break from all of that and read about Mike and Courtney's story. No! Don't get me wrong, I like Mike and Courtney but for now I'm more interested in Bobby's adventure. <br><br>Am I the only one who was still unclear about Saint Dane's whole plot? As I'm reading Saint Dane's evil plot reveal, I'm still like …....so you did ALL all that for THAT...I mean why did you make it so complicated dude?.... But I get it now, why Saint Dane did it the way he did, No, I don't think he was trying to impress Bobby, I think he wants to manipulate Bobby, forcing him to make a mistake by not sacrificing innocent lives. I think he wants Bobby to know that Bobby is still only a human with empathy and can't bring himself to do it when the time comes!! <br><br>You Evil Evil Man, Saint Dane<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506616518ra/24032562.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The short trip to Third World was AWESOME !! How I wish I can visit that earth too! I want to know if human race is family living in harmony and in good healthy ! I would love that library!! I mean the stark contrast between the First Earth was appalling. I wonder how Gunny survived the shock!<br><br>Ok just like I've predicted, Spader had his bitch fit again, I was so sure he believed Bobby at the gas station but when he ran off with the goon, I knew Spader is a lost cause, He can't see past his revenge, its sad because when Spader is not consumed by his hatred for Saint Dane, he is actually an awesome friend and perfect Traveler buddy. <br>I was very dissapointed when Spader did not trust Bobby and Gunny. I really did want to choke the living day lights out of him. I mean seriously why did he even doubt them ? Why was he perfectly fine trusting Bobby and Gunny but when he is in his bitch phase, he can't think straight......it must have hurt Bobby a lot!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506616518ra/24032564.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That time when Bobby had to decide if he should sacrifice lives and shoulder the responsibility for the rest of your life or don't do it, and face the desolation for many millennium to come!<br>I want Bobby to do it but at the same time I don't think I can do it myself. Sure, sacrifice a few to save many.......but that few's death is caused by your own hand!! ?? no wayyy arghhh<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464677968ra/19262200.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really want to go in detail with this book review but I feel like the whole book is a big puzzle and by revealing the twist here, it will really take away the mystery from the book. <br><br>I think I may have mentioned this before, but the whole “Idea” of Bobby coming back to Second Earth to see Mike and Courtney, while it was all great, I always feel like it takes a way the mystery of “unreachable and far away” vibe from the story. Because you get this impression that “Bobby can go back 'home' anytime”. But anyway, for this book Bobby's return revealed something storming up in Mike's head. I keep getting this idea that, Mike after reading about Spader and his adventure with Bobby, he wants to be apart of it. I get it, he has always been in the shadow of someone else, even though Bobby is far away, Mike is still somehow absorbing Bobby's aura and desperately hoping he too can be like Bobby. It's interesting to see how Mike's thinking had changes over years.<br><br>I'm curious to see Mike's development and his thoughts, I wonder if Mike's need for adventure and excitement will soon turn to jealousy and hate ?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494351529ra/22707361.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14103220181123836753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2439183271580081045">There are many types of themes and issues that are happening in “pendragon” right now. Here they are: Friendship issues, War vs. peace, Good vs. evil, and a bunch more. The main one for me though is Friendship issues. The main character, Bobby, and his friend, Spader, are having friendship issues. <br/><br/>Spader is mad at an evil guy named St. Dane for killing his father. Spader goes wild with anger when he hears about or sees St. Dane. This doesn’t help Bobby stop St. Dane from destroying Halla (Everyt</span>
  <span id="freeText2439183271580081045" style="display:none">There are many types of themes and issues that are happening in “pendragon” right now. Here they are: Friendship issues, War vs. peace, Good vs. evil, and a bunch more. The main one for me though is Friendship issues. The main character, Bobby, and his friend, Spader, are having friendship issues. <br /><br />Spader is mad at an evil guy named St. Dane for killing his father. Spader goes wild with anger when he hears about or sees St. Dane. This doesn’t help Bobby stop St. Dane from destroying Halla (Everything basically). Spader wanted to go with Bobby on his next adventure, and Bobby made Spader promise that he would listen to him when he said something and to control his temper. Spader promised and he went ahead, but constantly broke that promise. In the end, Spader almost ended up destroying Halla by not listening to Bobby.<br /><br />Bobby managed saving everything in the nick of time, but was mad at Spader for not listening to him. He tells Spader to go back to his home world, which is probably not the best for their friendship.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2839326444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2839326444" />
    <a title="~Cyanide Latte~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70514160-cyanide-latte"><img alt="~Cyanide Latte~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562894727p2/70514160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2839326444?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Cyanide Latte~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Cyanide Latte~" href="/user/show/70514160-cyanide-latte">~Cyanide Latte~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781416936275" href="/book/show/536978.The_Never_War">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">middle-grade sci-fi fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70514160-cyanide-latte?shelf=booktube-did-this-to-me">booktube-did-this-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70514160-cyanide-latte?shelf=pendragon-series">pendragon-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2839326444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11957572400909923718">When I was younger this was the book in the Pendragon series that kind of lost me. Anything with time travel as a theme tends to lose me before long because it's rarely done well. Time travel is one of those concepts that you can't mull over too deeply without it falling apart in most cases, because you'll start to see and pick apart the paradoxes and issues with it. As such, I never finished this book when I was younger, and intentionally kissed this series goodbye for a while.<br/><br/>Returning to this</span>
  <span id="freeText11957572400909923718" style="display:none">When I was younger this was the book in the Pendragon series that kind of lost me. Anything with time travel as a theme tends to lose me before long because it's rarely done well. Time travel is one of those concepts that you can't mull over too deeply without it falling apart in most cases, because you'll start to see and pick apart the paradoxes and issues with it. As such, I never finished this book when I was younger, and intentionally kissed this series goodbye for a while.<br /><br />Returning to this years later and being willing to suspend my disbelief a little further than I was before, I would say that for the most part, the time travel in this book was done well. (Given the fact that time between territories tends to be relative for Travelers, maybe that has something to do with it. Or it could really just be that I made it a point not to think too hard about the consequences of time traveling and changing the course of history.) Either way, this book was more enjoyable to read this time around, and I am able to appreciate the turns the story took.<br /><br />I've still got very mixed feelings about Bobby as our main character, but this book was needed, as it really forced him to mature in ways that he wouldn't have achieved otherwise if he hadn't faced the challenges that he did. I don't have much else to say beyond this, just know that the story holds up and has improved from the first two books, and I appreciated it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11957572400909923718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2377646940" />
    <a title="Mikkel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75949382-mikkel"><img alt="Mikkel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2377646940&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2377646940" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1310887022507540915"><br/><b>Introduction:</b><br/>Bobby and Spader, the Traveler from Cloral, arrive on Veelox a few weeks after the death of Bobby's uncle, Press Tilton, only to figure out from Aja Killian, the Traveler from Veelox, that Saint Dane went to First Earth. They flume there to be greeted by bullets from gangsters that Saint Dane has hired. They then met the First Earth Traveler, who saved them from the gangsters. He is a bell captain at the Manhattan Tower Hotel named Vincent. I found this book when I was looking aroun</span>
  <span id="freeText1310887022507540915" style="display:none"><br /><b>Introduction:</b><br />Bobby and Spader, the Traveler from Cloral, arrive on Veelox a few weeks after the death of Bobby's uncle, Press Tilton, only to figure out from Aja Killian, the Traveler from Veelox, that Saint Dane went to First Earth. They flume there to be greeted by bullets from gangsters that Saint Dane has hired. They then met the First Earth Traveler, who saved them from the gangsters. He is a bell captain at the Manhattan Tower Hotel named Vincent. I found this book when I was looking around the library. I had read the first two books and I have finished the third. I am looking forward to reading the rest of the books as I found the first two great books.<br /><br /><b>Summary:</b><br />The critical connection is revealed to be the Hindenburg zeppelin. To understand its significance, Bobby and Gunny (Vincent) visit Third Earth, in the 51st Century. The Traveler of Third Earth, Patrick, accesses a computer that predicts the future in which they save the Hindenburg: industrial spies working for Max would lead to the Nazis developing an atomic bomb and disastrously winning World War Two. Bobby and Gunny return to First Earth, only to find that Spader and Rose have gone ahead, seeking to stop Winn Farrow from shooting a firework rocket into Hindenburg.<br /><br /><b>Personal Opinion:</b><br />I honestly have really liked and enjoyed the Pendragon books so far, and I am looking forward to reading the rest of the books. I feel as this book was my favorite so far, since Bobby finally gets to reunite with his friends again, and then hang out for some time before having to go back to find out what Saint Dane is up to this time. You might like this book if you're really into Fantasy Fiction type of books. A lot of it can be a little confusing to follow for a bit, but it once you take the time to understand it, you can easily jump in and enjoy the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1310887022507540915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6339461068016565369">This plot was handled better than some of the other books, but the author's political views, such as environmentalism and "family planning" (in this particular sense it seems fairly likely that this is synonymous with massive abortion because it results in global population reaching zero growth) as the grounds for utopia come glaring through so much that the book is awful, and even delves into loss of personal humanity while the author tries to convince you it's okay. Imagine if three men were i</span>
  <span id="freeText6339461068016565369" style="display:none">This plot was handled better than some of the other books, but the author's political views, such as environmentalism and "family planning" (in this particular sense it seems fairly likely that this is synonymous with massive abortion because it results in global population reaching zero growth) as the grounds for utopia come glaring through so much that the book is awful, and even delves into loss of personal humanity while the author tries to convince you it's okay. Imagine if three men were in a room, Bill, Ted, and Jim. Imagine that a cement wall is about to collapse on them and kill all three men. However, you have knowledge of the probabilities of time and know that if you choose to shoot Ted in cold blood, Bill and Jim come out alive. This concept was shown perfectly in the two boats scenario of "The Dark Knight." It is better to die and allow someone else who is innocent to die than to kill someone innocent to prevent our deaths. It is the definition of our humanity, to put the morals of our consciousness above our own survival. When we are in the face of a situation where lives are on the line, it is our duty to save all that we can, but not by any means necessary. If the means are evil, so are the ends. You must find another way, not just assume that your choice is how things were meant to be.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15983522743944120658">Adult reread of Pendragon, part 3!!<br/><br/>Right, okay, so this reread hasn't been going well. But I actually thought this book had the strongest plot so far. Maybe it was because it takes place on First Earth and has immediate consequences for Second Earth (aka "our world"). I really liked the glimpse of Third Earth, and was actually surprised because I had forgotten that Third Earth had underground cities. That was a concept I included in my own writing, and until now I thought I'd made it up. I guess</span>
  <span id="freeText15983522743944120658" style="display:none">Adult reread of Pendragon, part 3!!<br /><br />Right, okay, so this reread hasn't been going well. But I actually thought this book had the strongest plot so far. Maybe it was because it takes place on First Earth and has immediate consequences for Second Earth (aka "our world"). I really liked the glimpse of Third Earth, and was actually surprised because I had forgotten that Third Earth had underground cities. That was a concept I included in my own writing, and until now I thought I'd made it up. I guess I'm not as original as I think I am.<br /><br />The one thing I found slightly unbelievable about this book was the fact that Third Earth is 3,000 years in the future, while Second Earth and First Earth are only like 70 years apart. That makes no sense! Either put First Earth further in the past (King Arthur era? that would be super cool) or make Third Earth only a couple hundred years in the future. A lot can change in a few hundred years! Three thousand years is a REALLY LONG TIME. It just seemed unnecessary.<br /><br />I was also bummed that we got almost no Mark &amp; Courtney time in this book! :( Bobby is slightly less of an idiot now that he's forced to be more independent, but he's still not my favorite character to follow around. Actually, Spader acted more like a moron in this one, which made me much sad. Hashtag problematic fave.<br /><br />On to book 4, I guess. Yay?</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2744167847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11450512519443949659">The Never War is the third book in the Pendragon series. The story starts off shortly after the death of Pendragon's Uncle Press. Pendragon and Spader travel to Veelox, only to find that Saint Dane has gone to first Earth. When they arrive at the first Earth flume, they are shot at by two gangsters in what seems to be the 1900s. The travelers escape the gangsters with the help of the first Earth traveler, Gunny Van Dyke. The travelers soon realizes that Saint Dane's plot on first Earth has somet</span>
  <span id="freeText11450512519443949659" style="display:none">The Never War is the third book in the Pendragon series. The story starts off shortly after the death of Pendragon's Uncle Press. Pendragon and Spader travel to Veelox, only to find that Saint Dane has gone to first Earth. When they arrive at the first Earth flume, they are shot at by two gangsters in what seems to be the 1900s. The travelers escape the gangsters with the help of the first Earth traveler, Gunny Van Dyke. The travelers soon realizes that Saint Dane's plot on first Earth has something to do with the Hindenburg blimp. The travel to third Earth (the future) to figure out Saint Dane's goal. Gunny and Pendragon realize that the Hindenburg must crash, but Spader, who they left back on first Earth, tries to save the Hindenburg. The first Earth plot ends with Gunny holding back Spader while Pendragon destroys the Hindenburg. I really love this book. It took an interesting twist on history, as well as many fantasy elements and made it into a fun, suspenseful book. I would recommend this book to everyone.</span>

      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8261480-jp?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2375417669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15063043544846147449"><blockquote><br/>“You want to know why we're the ones responsible?" Gunny asked.<br/><br/>I looked up into a pair of wise eyes that had seen far more than mine. <br/><br/>"Because there's nobody else," he said.<br/></blockquote><br/><br/>Well, now we know why 'our' Earth is called Second Earth. Turns out there is also a First Earth, which seems to be quite literally the past: specifically in the 1930s. Since we've been told a number of times that a traveler (somehow) always arrives when they need to, I'm not sure why these would be separate worlds at all, but</span>
  <span id="freeText15063043544846147449" style="display:none"><blockquote><br />“You want to know why we're the ones responsible?" Gunny asked.<br /><br />I looked up into a pair of wise eyes that had seen far more than mine. <br /><br />"Because there's nobody else," he said.<br /></blockquote><br /><br />Well, now we know why 'our' Earth is called Second Earth. Turns out there is also a First Earth, which seems to be quite literally the past: specifically in the 1930s. Since we've been told a number of times that a traveler (somehow) always arrives when they need to, I'm not sure why these would be separate worlds at all, but so it goes.<br /><br />The story itself is fairly interesting. It's much more grounded than what we saw on on Denduron or Coral, leaning on what that reader actually knows / has read previously about the 30s, including gangs and corruption throughout cities and the upcoming threat of World War II. I really like the ending, where (mostly avoiding spoilers) you end up with a somewhat standard time travel trouble of having to chose between the evil you know happened and possibly upsetting everything. <br /><br />Characterwise, I like the new traveler from First Earthy: Gunny. It's interesting to see a different, much older viewpoint on the whole thing, that still hasn't spent as much time around anything other than his own world. Spader returns from Cloral. Throughout most of the story, I like what I liked last time around: he's fun loving and competent. Towards the end though, we really get a taste of what I was worried about last time around: he's passionate to a fault, willing to sacrifice quite a lot to do what he believes needs to be done--even when people he should trust tell him otherwise. <br /><br />So it goes. <br /><br />I don't like this as much as the previous stories. It's a combination of time travel just not feeling like it makes sense / something that's needed in a universe like this + the aforementioned issues with Spader. Looks like he'll be taking the next book off though, so onward we go! It's still a fun enough read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15063043544846147449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17067524682355826880">Another great sequel to fit perfectly into the series flow. It was just as satisfying as I remember it when I read it the first time.<br/><br/>I think what is especially special about this one is Bobby’s growth as he becomes determined to keep up his Traveler work, as well as his interactions with Saint Dane, when the demon reveals the actual, ruthless reasons for his plotting. <br/><br/>My first look at the book made me feel like it would be boring because of the historical fiction angle. But it adds in SciFi and </span>
  <span id="freeText17067524682355826880" style="display:none">Another great sequel to fit perfectly into the series flow. It was just as satisfying as I remember it when I read it the first time.<br /><br />I think what is especially special about this one is Bobby’s growth as he becomes determined to keep up his Traveler work, as well as his interactions with Saint Dane, when the demon reveals the actual, ruthless reasons for his plotting. <br /><br />My first look at the book made me feel like it would be boring because of the historical fiction angle. But it adds in SciFi and brings everything together so concisely that you really get to enjoy the ride again. Having Mark and Courtney read it all at once is a bonus too, so that this books format goes straight through the journals. Just as great as the last two!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j2Pnv718Syfs9bwJFaXVxoW8qOH3lo3BZ7tSOQEFcZ520G9ir8DMDobe2BLCZhYDG2Hkh7tOPmNRs5FHbiN1jA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JAiRKYGx5qgwq8eFgTzgGwpxhtNFja8vzwifQC5Vz+bduxn0kw1hgVqAo55W/yPelKzKtQlVHI35AFw+QXPL9A==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/74046.D_J_MacHale">About D.J. MacHale</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/74046.D_J_MacHale"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1418514923p3/74046.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12282442281576840611">D.J. MacHale is a writer, director, executive producer and creator of several popular television series and movies.<br/><br/>He was raised in Greenwich, CT and graduated from Greenwich High School. While in school, he had several jobs including collecting eggs at a poultry farm, engraving sports trophies and washing dishes in a steakhouse...in between playing football and running track. D.J. then attended N</span>
  <span id="freeText12282442281576840611" style="display:none">D.J. MacHale is a writer, director, executive producer and creator of several popular television series and movies.<br /><br />He was raised in Greenwich, CT and graduated from Greenwich High School. While in school, he had several jobs including collecting eggs at a poultry farm, engraving sports trophies and washing dishes in a steakhouse...in between playing football and running track. D.J. then attended New York University where he received a BFA in film production.<br /><br />His filmmaking career began in New York where he worked as a freelance writer/director, making corporate videos and television commercials. He also taught photography and film production.<br /><br />D.J. broke into the entertainment business by writing several ABC Afterschool Specials. After moving to Los Angeles, he made the fulltime switch from informational films, to entertainment. As co-creator of the popular Nickelodeon series: Are You Afraid of the Dark?, he produced all 91 episodes over 8 years. He wrote and directed many of the episodes including the CableAce nominated The Tale of Cutter's Treasure starring Charles S. Dutton. He was nominated for a Gemini award for directing The Tale of the Dangerous Soup starring Neve Campbell.<br /><br />D.J. also wrote and directed the movie Tower of Terror for ABC's Wonderful World of Disney which starred Kirsten Dunst and Steve Guttenberg. The Showtime series Chris Cross was co-created, written and produced by D.J. It received the CableAce award for Best Youth Series.<br /><br />D.J. co-created and produced the Discovery Kids series Flight 29 Down for which he writes all the episodes and directs several. His work on Flight 29 Down has earned him both Writers Guild of America and Directors Guild of America award nominations.<br /><br />Other notable writing credits include the classic ABC Afterschool Special titled Seasonal Differences; the pilot for the long-running PBS/CBS series Ghostwriter; and the HBO series Encyclopedia Brown, Boy Detective for which he received a CableAce nomination for writing.<br /><br />In print, D.J. has co-written the book The Tale of the Nightly Neighbors, based on his own teleplay and penned the poetic adaptation of the classic Norwegian folk tale East of the Sun and West of the Moon.<br /><br />The book series: Pendragon - Journal of an Adventure through Time and Space marks D.J.'s first turn as a novelist. He plans for this series of Young Adult adventures to span a total of 10 books.<br /><br />D.J. lives in Southern California with his wife Evangeline and daughter Keaton. They are avid backpackers, scuba divers and skiers. Rounding out the household are a Golden Retriever, Maggie; and a Kitten, Kaboodle. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12282442281576840611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
